< text>
Several years ago, the exhaust pipe on my '95 Del Sol Vtec got snapped on the freeway due to debris I couldn't avoid.  Concord Honda wanted to charge me 350.00 just to tell me they couldn't do the repair.  I asked my chiropractor, Dr. William Haley (who's awesome) who he could recommend to repair my car.  Without hesitation, he recommended West Coast Muffler, and said they had done wonderful work on his cars.  I called them, and had my car towed there.  Apparently, my car originally had a curved pipe leading to the muffler.  I got a call about an hour after they got my car, and I was told they could custom make another curved pipe, but that it would be far cheaper, and just as stable, for them to put on a straight pipe. The difference in price was about 400.00.  They could have just done the more expensive job.  I wouldn't have known any better.  But they gave me an option, so I of course took the less expensive route.  I've never had any problems with the replacement pipe, and I recommend their shop to anyone who will listen.  Thanks again for the great work, great customer service, and most of all, the great ethics.<//text>

<Review>Not a bad spot for clay rice pot. I've driven by this restaurant for so many years without realizing what they served here. I came to know the name thanks to the sisters from HangryDiary when they mentioned this restaurant is their favorite for rice pot. Hailing from Hong Kong, I love all types of clay rice pots, especially the crispy rice on the bottom. So going into Nature Pagoda, I had high expectations as to their taste.

I came here alone on a Monday afternoon and it was very quiet. There were only 2 other tables occupied by groups but the workers had a lot of time on their hands. I ordered their lunch portion preserved meat rice pot, which also came with a small soup. I don't know the exact name but it tasted a lot like chicken soup with winter melon but I could be wrong. Once the pot came out, I waited a couple minutes before digging in because I wanted the rice at the bottom to get even crisipier so that I can struggle and dig for it at the end of the meal.

Overall taste was just okay; the soy sauce they provided was more on the salty side and not sweet enough. Soy sauce for this dish needs to be dark and sweet in order to fully enjoy it. The amount of meat was less than abundant but then again, it was a lunch portion. The part I was longing for was a disappointment though. Not enough crispy rice at the end but there still was some so enjoy at least, which is why I gave this place a four. I honestly believe I would come back and try other dishes in the future but I'll just stick to a different restaurant for my clay rice pots because I get a lot more crispy rice.<//Review>< time>

<Rate>4< /Rate><review>The park has a small parking lot, and considering it's in a neighborhood I can only imagine how packed it will get on the weekends.  The park is made of four yards; the children's park, and three yards for dogs.
The largest is for large dogs. Nice running area.
The second smallest is for small dogs.
And the third is the agility yard.

The expectations I had were low since most parks in the contra costa area are left to turn into garbage and filled with fox tails which are very dangerous for dogs.

The park is near a dump of property which brings my concern of rodents that will most likely cause holes in the lawns.

My concern is how people didn't bother to ask if they can bring in their larger dogs into the agility yard when there's small dogs in there.

And the most disappointing issue I have for the summer is there's NO SHADE. In the heat how could they not plan for shade in the summer??

The park is pretty and large- I'm pretty happy with the size of the small dog yard as they usually get stuck with less than a quarter of what large dogs get. My dogs love running and seeing them take off in the park was fun.

Mostly I have concerns about the lack of shade.< /review>< pictures>

<username>Tim Burgess< /username><Date>1530468450267< /Date><rate>3< /rate>< Text>
One way gates are a problem waiting to happen. Someone will be injured in these gates as they are now configured.
Dog litter bag dispensers should be inside the play areas not outside, same for the garbage cans.
Bolts sticking up on the agility play structure, hidden by bark, dangerous for people and dogs.
The agility ramps on the structure are slick and too steep.
As mentioned in other reviews, the distinction between agility area, small dog area, large dog area is blurred and invites injury to small dogs. Why not put a second agility setup in the large dog area too?
Need to install shade structures similar to the ones in Brentwood dog parks. There is zero shade.<//Text>

<text>I was craving Brazilian food, specifically, feijoada, so I decided to stop by Pedro's Brazil Cafe for the first time. Unfortunately, the meats were chewy, dry, and hardly had flavor. The rice also tasted like it came from a boil-in-a-bag, or it was microwaved rice. Additionally, the service was not great. I sat down and waited for ten minutes - I wasn't greeted or even acknowledged. But I may have come in at a bad time. People were switching shifts (It was at around 5 PM). <Review>I've been coming here ever since my days at Cal. This is one of the places where I'd come to forget my sinking GPA, my overdue assignments, my bank balance and literally all misery of my life.

Sitting out in the sun on the patio at the back, on a Saturday, eating some warm and comforting feijoada and sipping on the cool mango slushies was as good as it got.

Ever since the Butcher's son moved next door, I've seen a lot less traffic here. In its heyday, feijoada would be over before 1 in the afternoon! It was that popular! I started receiving care form Dr. Markham about 8 years ago and really liked him.  A few years back he doubled his office size and I immediately began to see a decline in the quality of care my family and I were receiving.  There were multiple staff changes during this time as well.  Things really got bad a year ago when we put my daughter in braces. This resulted in many return trips to his office to have procedures repaired or redone completely.  Brackets and wires would constantly come undone, sometimes within hours of leaving the office.  The final straw was the arrival of his new receptionist, Heather. To add to my frustration, my family and I recently began seeing a new dentist and found that procedures done within the last 6 months by Dr. Markham and his staff have to be repaired or completely redone, resulting in an added expense.  I still, after 8 years of continuous business, have not received even a text from Dr. Markham to address any of my concerns.
